..................................................................................................................10a\n\nn\nmotio\ncom/\ns.\nbrief\n.tech\nwww\n\nSupplement to NASA Tech Briefs\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nToC\n\n+\n\n\xe2\x80\x93\n\nA\n\n\xe2\x9e\xad\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\nHigh-Temperature\nActuators for Aircraft\nPropulsion Systems\n\nF\n\nuture \xe2\x80\x9cmore electric aircraft\xe2\x80\x9d\n(MEA) will require electric actuation systems for control surfaces\nand engine controls. Electric motors,\ndrive electronics, and mechanisms are\nessential elements of aircraft actuation\nin MEAs that incorporate ElectroMagnetic Actuators (EMAs). High-temperature environments experienced in\naircraft applications place demands on\nactuator components, materials, and\ninsulation systems that dictate the use of\nnew technologies and materials.\nHigh Temperature Electromagnetic\nActuator (HTEMA) options for hightemperature aircraft environments\ninclude appropriate motor types, drive\nand control electronics, mechanisms,\nmaterials, and construction methods.\nThese options are evaluated to identify\ncandidates that meet the challenges of\ntomorrow\xe2\x80\x99s MEA actuators.\nEfforts to design, build, and test a prototype demonstrating a high-temperature, high-reliability class of all-electromagnetic actuator design with minimal/no heat load on aircraft cooling systems are ongoing. Size and weight goals\nare consistent with the aircraft engine\nlimits. The key technical aspects being\naddressed include operation in the high\ntemperature and vibration environment, actuator force, power, weight, size,\nefficiency, speed, stroke, mechanical\nrobustness and reliability, lifecycle cost,\nfailure modes and effects, and maintenance predictions.\nEngine nozzle actuation is presently\naccomplished using fuel as a hydraulic\nworking fluid (fueldraulic actuation) for\nthe current-generation engine actuators. While the nozzle actuation has a\nlow duty cycle, the heat generated is continuous and presents a significant load\non the ircraft/engine thermal management system.\nAn electrically driven actuator can\nreduce the heat load of the aircraft. The\n\nFigure 1: HTEMA actuator package (left) and interior view.\n\npresent engine fueldraulic actuators and\naircraft fuel systems are highly interrelated, leading to a challenging thermal management problem that has an\nimpact on aircraft performance.\nElimination of this fuel heat load\nreduces the fuel system\xe2\x80\x99s thermal issues.\nHigh-temperature,\nelectromagnetic\nactuator component solutions that meet\nthe technology challenges and performance requirements for an actuator system operating engine nozzle actuation\nhave been identified.\n\nConvergent Nozzle Actuation\nThe design and development of\nHTEMA technology for a Convergent\nNozzle Actuation System (CNAS) actuator has been completed. The CNAS is\nthe first critical application of the\nHTEMA technology, providing the\npower to position the nozzle as required\nfor the pilot-selected engine Power Level\nAngle (PLA). The CNAS actuators are\nmounted to the aft end of the engine.\nCurrent fueldraulic actuators for the\nCNAS are limited by the actuator O-ring\nmaterial. In the CNAS application, fluid\ntemperature limits approach 325 \xc2\xb0F and\n\nIIa\n\nwww.techbriefs.com/motion\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nToC\n\n+\n\nseal temperature limits approach 400 \xc2\xb0F.\nThe current engine actuators are able to\noperate in a temperature environment\napproaching 325 \xc2\xb0F continually and up\nto 560 \xc2\xb0F for transients of 10 seconds by\nusing the hydraulic fluid (fuel) as a\nmeans of cooling.\nThe CNAS actuators have a linear\nstroke of 4", a combined stall load (for 4\nactuators) of 42,000 lbf, and weigh\nabout 52 lbm (actuation system hardware including routing). Envelope goals\nprovided by the AFRL are 11 \xc3\x97 2.5 \xc3\x97 6.5".\nThe power type is 270 VDC.\nKey technologies evaluated included\nmotor, insulation, bearings, electronics,\ngearing, cooling, and signals and sensors\nfor a notional actuator. The best candidates for detailed design and optimization were identified.\nThe notional CNAS HTEMA employs\nfive actuators, each capable of 10,500 lbs\n(46.7 kN) of force, producing a total of\n42,000 lbs (186.8 kN) with one actuator\nmissing. Given the requirement for an\nelectromagnetic solution, a direct drive\nactuator was considered first. Aerospace\nmachines typically develop a pressure of\n3-5 psi2 in the air gap due to magnetic\n\nMotion Control and Automation Technology, June 2014\n\n\xe2\x80\x93\n\nA\n\n\xe2\x9e\xad\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\n\xc2\xae\n\nNEW! Dualvee\nVacuum Wheels\nThe NEW Dualvee\xc2\xae Stainless Vacuum Wheels are specifically designed for use in vacuum environments. Dualvee Stainless\nVacuum Wheels are ideally suited for guided motion within vacuum environments such as automated material handling\nand manipulation equipment, sliding racks for loading and unloading, loadlock and transfer systems, and other custom\npositioning mechanisms.\n\nDownload our FREE datasheet for more product information\nwww2.bwc.com/vacuumwheels\n\nStop by Booth #2751\nJune 10-12, 2014 New York, NY\n\nGROUP\n\n(888) 580-8272\n\nwww.bwc.com\n\nBishop-Wisecarver Group is a WBENC certi\xef\xac\x81ed woman-owned\nfamily of companies who work with manufacturers to engineer,\nmanufacture, and build linear and rotary motion solutions, custom\ncomplex assemblies, and optimal embedded intelligence systems.\n\xc2\xa9 copyright 2014 Bishop-Wisecarver\n\nFree Info at http://info.hotims.com/49746-770\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nToC\n\n+\n\n\xe2\x80\x93\n\nA\n\n\xe2\x9e\xad\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\nHigh-Temperature Actuators\nfields. This dictates a gap area of at least\n2.1 \xc3\x97 103 square inches is needed to generate the required force. Based on the 5\npsi curve, an actuator with an 18" gap\ndiameter has roughly a 2\' outer diameter\nand 3\' length. An approximate actuator\nweight would be greater than 1,000\npounds, which is clearly unacceptable.\nGiven the envelope requirement of\n11 \xc3\x97 2.5 \xc3\x97 6.5", an 11"-long machine\nwould have over a 60" diameter, an unacceptable result.\nTherefore, the CNAS application\nrequires mechanical advantage to\ndecrease the required electromagnetic\nactuator force and size, while increasing\nspeed. The Navy investigated electromagnetic actuator replacements for\nhydraulic cylinders and found planetary\nroller screws to be a good candidate for\nrotor-to-linear conversion and mechanical advantage. Typical COTS roller\nscrew ratings indicate a screw diameter\nin the 30- to 48-mm (~1.2 to 1.9") range\nis appropriate.\nInclusion of a single-pass, 5 to 1 planetary gear between the planetary roller\nscrew and motor improves this situation. COTS planetary gears show a significant performance advantage for a\n\nsmall weight (<2.8 lbs). Issues with dry\nlubrication, life, and seals must be\naddressed in a custom detailed design\nfor this high-temperature application.\nHowever, this information is sufficient\nfor trade studies. Assuming a ~3:1\nlength-to-diameter ratio, the motor\nweight is less than 12 pounds.\nHarmonic drives were considered for\nhigher gear ratios in smaller packages.\nHowever, concerns about the ability to\nback-drive the unit in some failure\nmodes prevented inclusion in the baseline design. Magnetic gearing is also an\noption but concerns about permanent\nmagnet (PM) demagnetization during\nflux reversals at high temperature were\nconsidered high risk.\nCare must be exercised in the lead\nscrew and gear ratio selection if the\nactuator must be back-driven with the\npower off. There is a critical angle in\nlead screws where the unit will act as a\nfriction lock at and below the critical\nvalue. Similarly, the gearing will multiply any drag and cogging torques present in the motor, which can also inhibit\nthe ability to back-drive an actuator. It is\nimportant to keep this in mind during\ndetailed trades.\n\nBaseline Actuator Concept\nThe system design includes the following key components and technologies:\nroller screw, planetary gearing, hightemperature coatings, high-temperature\nmotor materials and insulation system,\nhigh-temperature power electronics,\nand sensors.\nSeveral motor types have been considered with high efficiency and minimal weight and volume. These include\nsurface mount PM, Halbach Array PM,\nburied magnet PM, and hybrid stepper.\nOthers that do not require PMs\ninclude wound rotor DC (brush and\nbrushless), variable or switched reluctance (VR or SR) machines, and squirrel cage induction motors. Trades have\nidentified brushless DC PM and SR\nmachines are of primary interest. Both\nmotors can use sensorless commutation methods. A VR resolver can be\nincorporated in the design if required\nfor control feedback.\nVR motors are robust with simple\nwindings, facilitating application of\nhigh-temperature insulation. Because\nVR motors have no permanent magnets,\nthey do not generate a back Electro\nMotive Force (EMF) voltage when\n\nFigure 2: HTEMA representation in Simulink.\n\n2a\n\nwww.techbriefs.com/motion\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nToC\n\n+\n\nMotion Control and Automation Technology, June 2014\n\n\xe2\x80\x93\n\nA\n\n\xe2\x9e\xad\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\nFree Info at http://info.hotims.com/49\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nToC\n\n+\n\n-\n\n\xe2\x80\x93\n\nA\n\n\xe2\x9e\xad\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\nHigh-Temperature Actuators\nunpowered, which may be advantageous\nin some failure modes.\nThe PM motor design includes a band\nto contain the surface-mount PMs. VR\nmachines do not require such containment requirements, but have quite small\nmechanical gaps that must be maintained over temperature and life. Both\nmachines can be back-driven, with VR\nmachines having an advantage of no\nback EMF generated when unpowered.\nThis may be an advantage in failure\nmodes and effects analyses (FMEA).\nGiven the motor is used in an aircraft\n\napplication, high-saturation flux density\nlamination material is highly desirable.\nBrushless DC PM motors provide\nexcellent efficiency with high bandwidth\nfor servo applications. Brushless commutation is appropriate for life, reliability, and maintenance issues. High motor\npole count is a big factor in minimizing\nweight. Maximum slew rate, speed,\nswitching speed, and/or geometry will\nbe the limiting factor, but the higher the\nnumber of poles, the better.\nMechanical gears are a mature technology with a long and rich history.\n\nMachined Springs\n& Flexible Couplings\n\nTradition + Innovation = Solutions\n\nFollowing 55 successful years in business, Helical Products\nCompany, Inc. and its engineering team have developed\nextensive experience designing and manufacturing innovative\nproducts for controlling mechanical movements, specializing in\n\ncustomers served, why not let Helical spring into action and start\ncoupling your dreams with reality today!\n\nor a\natalog\nfree c s today at:\nFor a\nail u\nm\nle, em heli-cal.co\nsamp\nst@\nque\nfreere\n\nMotion Control and Automation Technology, June 2014\n\nFree Info at http://info.hotims.com/49746-772\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\n4a\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nToC\n\nWhen properly designed, applied, and\nmaintained, they can provide long, failure-free performance. In addition, cost\nand manpower limitations are pushing\nhardware toward more robust, no-maintenance technologies.\nPlanetary gears were selected in the\nbaseline design for their power-dense,\nhigh-torque transmission capacity and\nform factor. A COTS gearhead was identified with 5:1 gear ratio in a single pass.\nModifications to the COTS gearhead\nwith a 98- 95% efficiency for a single pass\nand 150,000 to 200,000 hours of life at\nroom temperature to meet the hightemperature environment are anticipated. Flex spline or harmonic drives can\nalso be used if failure modes and effects\nanalyses show their inability to be backdriven is not an issue.\nA simulation study of HTEMA was performed based on flow-down requirements. The simulation tool used was\nSimulink\ntogether\nwith\nits\nSimPowerSystems (SPS) toolbox from\nMathWorks. Instead of using SPS library\nmodels, custom models were created for\nthe permanent magnet synchronous\nmotor, the motor drive, and some of the\nmechanical elements. The main reason\nfor creating custom models is that the\nexisting SPS models do not provide the\nflexibility needed for detailed study of\nthe HTEMA.\nAs shown in Figure 2, a nested controller structure is used to provide the\nservo performance. The outermost control loop is the position controller,\nwhich generates the motor speed reference used by the speed controller. The\nspeed controller calculates the motor\ncurrent reference, and the innermost\ncurrent controller regulates the motor\ncurrent to follow this reference.\nKey elements of the HTEMA have\nbeen investigated, and the baseline\ndesign meets the space, weight, and performance requirements. Development\ncontinues to mature the HTEMA system\nfor the CNAS application, perform\ndetailed design, build and test a prototype unit, and validate analytical models. This work will lead to efforts that\ntransition the HTEMA to military flightcertified hardware supporting future\nengine upgrades and commercial aviation applications.\nThis article was written by Gerald Foshage,\nRichard Young, Yuntao Xu, Edward Wagner,\nand Dennis Mahoney of RCT Systems\n(Linthicum Heights, MD); and Alireza R.\nBehbahani of the Air Force Research\nLaboratory. The desired\npattern data covers a hemisphere above\nthe antenna of interest, which is close to\nthe ground. This is incompatible with\ntraditional measurements that place the\n\nantenna under test on a movable support that tilts and rotates.\nThe solution is to suspend the probe\nfrom three or more flexible cables\nattached to computer-controlled winches that are supported above the test volume. By varying the length of the cables,\nthe position of the probe can be moved\n\nOEM-priced NFPA Air Cylinders\n\nShipping in 2 days!\nNew NFPA cylinders\nincorporate important\noptions at no extra cost\nStandard features include:\nAnodized aluminum end caps\n303 Hard chrome plated shaft\nAdjustable air cushions both ends\nStainless steel tie rods\nMagnetic pistons\nSpecial rod bushings provide\nself lubrication of piston rods\nFactory lube is Magnalube-G\xc2\xae\n3D CAD drawings\nWant more information?\nScan here for a PDF catalog.\n\nInterchangeability as expected with a wide range of NFPA mounting options\nw w w . f a b c o - a i r. c o m\ntel: (352) 373-3578\nSolving pneumatic problems since 1958. Let us help !\n\nMotion Control and Automation Technology, June 2014\n\nFree Info at http://info.hotims.com/49746-774\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\n6a\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nToC\n\nanywhere in the test volume. A separate\nmetrology system can be used to\nincrease the accuracy of knowledge of\nthe probe position and orientation.\nThe probe carrier, at the junction of\nthe suspension cables, has actuators to\nalter the probe orientation. Power is\nsupplied by passing current through\nthe suspension cables, or by battery\npower on the probe carrier. Multiple\nsets of cables and probe platforms can\nbe used to simulate multiple orbiting\nassets. The probe can be a transmitter,\na receiver, or both, and can be at any\nfrequency that is needed for the test\nscenario. A calibration reference, for\nphase and/or amplitude, can be transmitted to the probe carrier by RF, optical, or wired means.\nThis technology has been used to \xe2\x80\x9cfly\xe2\x80\x9d\na video or film camera over a football\nstadium, but has never been used for\nantenna measurements or simulation of\nmoving sources over an area. For lowprecision applications, the lengths of the\ncables can be mathematically transformed into the position of the probe.\nAn external tracking system, using optical or RF means, can be used for higher\nprecision. Closed loop control can be\nimplemented from the tracking system\nto the winch controllers to allow very\nprecise and repeatable control of the\nposition of the probe.\nThe cables can be made of any reasonably strong material, although materials with low elasticity (e.g. Kevlar or\nSpectra) are preferred for precision\npositioning. Steel cables have been used\nin the commercial flying camera applications. However, a non-conductive\ncable has significant advantages for the\nantenna and RF application, since it\ndoes not perturb the RF fields as much\nas a conductive cable; however, with\nsuitable probe design, a conductive\ncable may be acceptable. Non-conductive cables improve safety, since the\ncables won\xe2\x80\x99t conduct dangerous voltages or currents, as from an inadvertent\ncontact with some energized conductor\nor lightning.\nPower for the probe is provided either\nby batteries, solar cells, or other means.\nIf it is desired to use conductive support\ncables, they can be used to carry power.\nIn this case, the addition of suitable RF\nabsorbing materials may be needed to\n\n+\n\n\xe2\x80\x93\n\nA\n\n\xe2\x9e\xad\n\nreduce the effect on the measurement\naccuracies. Control and telemetry signals from the moving probe can be carried by an optical fiber or other wireless\nmeans. While three cables are the minimum to provide the desired positioning,\n\nthe use of more cables can provide a\nwider range of motion, and can allow\npositioning of the orientation of the\nprobe.\nThis work was done by James P. Lux of\nCaltech for NASA\xe2\x80\x99s Jet Propulsion Laboratory.\n\nFor more information, download the\nTechnical Support Package (free white\npaper) at www.techbriefs.com/tsp under the\nMechanics/Machinery category. NPO-44090\n\nFluidic Actuators with No Moving Parts\nLangley Research Center, Hampton, Virginia\nTwo new fluidic actuator designs were\ndeveloped to control fluid flow in ways\nthat will ultimately result in improved system performance and fuel efficiency in\ntoimprove the aerodynamic performance\nof a variety of vehicles. These flow control\nactuators, often referred to as fluidic oscillators or sweeping jet actuators, utilize the\nCoanda effect to generate spatially oscillating bursts (or jets). They can be embedded directly into a control surface (such\nas a wing or a turbine blade) to help\nreduce flow separation, increase lift,\nreduce drag, enhance mixing, or increase\nheat transfer. Recent studies show up to a\n60% performance enhancement (such as\nincreased lift or reduced drag) with fluidic actuators.\n\nOne of the actuator designs effectively\ndecouples the oscillation frequency from\nthe amplitude (i.e. mass flow through the\nactuator). A decoupled actuator can deliver\nhigh mass flow rates without changing the\nfrequency, or deliver high- or low-frequency\noscillating jets at minimal mass flow rates.\nThe second actuator design enables inphase or anti-phase synchronization of the\noscillating jets. This overcomes issues\ncaused by the random oscillation of individual actuators when they are used in an array\nof actuators, and has particular benefit for\nflow-control applications. These new\ndesigns will provide better control authority\nover the fluidic actuator, increased actuator\nefficiency, decreased mass flow, and\nimproved system performance.\n\nMotion Control and Automation Technology, June 2014\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nThe new actuator designs do not\nrequire any additional equipment\xe2\x80\x94\noscillations, decoupling, and synchronization are achieved in a passive manner, entirely via internal flow dynamics.\nSince these actuators have simple and\ncompact structure and do not have any\nmoving parts, they are basically maintenance-free, and highly scalable. They\ncan be manufactured from many different materials and therefore can also be\nused in harsh environments.\nThis work was done by Mehti Koklu of\nLangley Research Center. For more information, download the Technical Support Package\n(free white paper) at www.techbriefs.com/tsp\nunder the Mechanics/Machinery category.\nLAR-18089-1/90-1\n\n7a\n\nFree Info at http://info.hotims.com/49746-775\n\nToC\n\n+\n\n\xe2\x80\x93\n\nA\n\n\xe2\x9e\xad\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\nApplications\nSubmersible Pressure Transducer for Tank Fluid\nLevel Monitoring\nliquid can\nMonitoring the level ofdensityuse ofbea\naccomplished through the\npressure transducer. The\nof the\nliquid and its height create pressure on\nthe diaphragm of the pressure transducer to generate an accurate and cost-effective level measurement. Generally, pressure transducers can be used for level\nmeasurement from 10 inches of water\ncolumn up to 10,000 PSI (700 bar).\nDesigned with stainless steel and\nHytrel materials, submersible pressure\ntransducers are reliable, cost-effective\ninstruments to measure the level of various liquids including water and diesel.\nThese pressure sensors are an ideal\nchoice for mobile applications such as\nships, train cars, or when the tank is\ntransported between locations such as\nfor construction sites, chemical totes for\nindustrial processing, or well site injection chemicals.\nA variety of factors should be considered when installing a submersible pressure transducer in a tank. The figure\nshows one installation method used by\nAmerican Sensor Technologies for its\nAST4510 submersible transducer using\na rigid pipe. The transducer comes standard with a 1/2" NPT male conduit connection at the base of the cable connection. In tanks that are turbulent due to\nan inlet/fill pipe or the use of an agitator, the transducer can have rigid plastic\nor metal conduit installed over the\ncable to prevent sensor movement within the tank.\nThe conduit over the cable is mounted to a bung at the top of the tank. Parts\nthat thread onto a 1.5" female NPT\nbung and have a 1/2" female NPT\nthread can mate the ridid conduit. The\ncable exits the tank and is held in place\nby a cord grip that runs to the control\nbox. The same cable grip can be used at\nthe junction box, ensuring that the vent\ntube is clear. Depending on hazardous\nlocation requirements, this can be in the\n\nnon-hazardous area with connection to\nthe intrinsically safe barrier. In this\nexample, it is expected that the junction\nbox is properly vented to the atmosphere to prevent water ingress.\nIn this application, the pressure sensor was installed above the base of the\nbottom of the tank. As sludge and silt\ntend to line the bottom of the tank, a\nheight of 100 millimeters was calculated\nto ensure the process connection did\nnot clog over time. The diaphragm of\nthe transducer is close to the top of the\nprocess connection hex, so operators\ncan calculate the offset from when the\ntank is empty.\n\n8a\n\nwww.techbriefs.com/motion\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nToC\n\n+\n\nOther applications may have the submersible pressure transducer installed\ndirectly into an intrinsically safe radio\ndevice at the top of the tank. This\nreduces the cost of the transducer, as\nless cable and less time are required for\nthe installation. With shorter cable\nlengths, a voltage output signal with low\ncurrent consumption is an option if the\nsystem is battery operated. Less current\nconsumption means longer battery life\nand less maintenance.\nThis article was contributed by American\nSensor Technologies (AST), Mount Olive, NJ.\nFor more information, visit http://info.\nhotims.com/49746-322.\n\nMotion Control and Automation Technology, June 2014\n\n\xe2\x80\x93\n\nA\n\n\xe2\x9e\xad\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\nWhy Lin?\n\nThe Step Motor Specialists\n\nWhy Every Day More Engineers\nChoose Lin Engineering\nOver the past decade, Lin Engineering has\ngained a tremendous amount of market\nshare and earned a reputation as the\n\xe2\x80\x9cLeader in Step Motor Technology.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\nProven Application Support,\nPerformance, and Quality\n\nExtensive Product Line\n& Value Added Services\n\nUnrivaled Application Support\n\nStepper Motors ranging from NEMA 8 to NEMA 34\n\n98% application success rate\n95% of prototypes shipped in less than 1 week\n\nThe most complete line of high accuracy and low\nresonance 0.9 degree stepper motors\nValue added options such as: configurable shafts,\n\nHigh Performance\n\nwindings, and cable assemblies\n\nHighest torque output\nHigh accuracy = no skipping steps\nReduced vibration and resonance\n\nStepper Motors for vacuum, laboratory, and\nwash-down environments\n\nReliable Quality\nConsistent Performance\n4.5 Sigma System\nISO 9001 certified\nContinuous Improvement\n\nSatisfied Customers\n\nCustomers in 2004\n\nCustomers in 2014\n\n16245 Vineyard Blvd., Morgan Hill, CA 95037\nTel. The\nabsolute rotary encoder measures absolute angular position from 0\xc2\xb0 to 360\xc2\xb0 via programmable 13-bit (8,192\ncount) or 14-bit (13,950 count) resolution at\nspeeds exceeding 2500 rpm. System firmware\nalso tracks turns up to 12 bits (4096 revolutions).\nThe controller features multiple built-in interfaces: SSI, USB, RS485 Serial, Modbus RTU, two\nanalog outputs (4-20mA and \xc2\xb110V), and two digital set points.\nThe position sensor is an all-optical design that resists electromagnetic interference such as\nlightning, radiation, magnetic fields, and other harsh environmental conditions. It uses an optical technique embedded in a passive sensor and active controller connected by a duplex fiber\noptic link. The controller transmits a burst of light to the code disk in the sensor that modulates\nthe spectral components of the light based on angular position. Amplitude response of \xc2\xb15%\nis 1 to 10,000 Hz. The stud-mounted accelerometers have a 10-32\nthreaded hole. The Model 41A mounting bottom is a hex with 10-32\ntop connector; Model 42A mounting bottom is hex with 10-32 side\nconnector; and Model 43A has a cube shape that allows mounting in\ntwo different orientations, with the sensitive axis parallel to the connector and 10-32 connector. Optional accessories include cables, adhesive mounting adapter, and signal conditioners.\nThe Model 45A is a general-purpose, high-sensitivity triaxial\naccelerometer in a 20-mm cube shape with 500 mV/g (10 g range) and\n1000 mV/g (5 g range) options. Amplitude response of \xc2\xb15% is 1 to\n6000 Hz for y- and z-axes, and 1 to 3000 Hz for x-axis. They are also\nstud-mounted with a 10-32 threaded hole.\n\nTrio Motion Technology (Freeport, PA) has\nintroduced the MC403-Z motion controller in two versions offering\ncontrol of two or three axes. The\ncore axis connections can be configured as pulse and direction outputs to drives, or as incremental\nencoder feedback inputs or simulated\nencoder outputs. The three-axis variant\nallows one axis to be set-up as an extended axis where the connection may also be configured as an input for\nSSI, Tamagawa, or EnDAT absolute encoders.\nThe controllers feature a 64-bit ARM11 processor, digital and analog\nI/O count, built-in Ethernet, and the ability to add robotic transformations or synchronize motion with double floating point precision. The\ncontroller can undertake linear, circular, helical, and spherical interpolation across all axes, as well as flexible CAM shapes and linked\nmotion. The controller has eight 24 VDC digital inputs including six\n20-\xce\xbcsec registration inputs, and four 24 VDC bi-directional I/Os. Two\n12-bit analog inputs are included, and an RJ45 Ethernet port is provided for programming and connection of HMI or other devices.\n\nFor Free Info Visit http://info.hotims.com/49746-318\n\nFor Free Info Visit http://info.hotims.com/49746-328\n\nEtherCAT Drive Modules\nACS Motion Control (Bloomington, MN)\nhas introduced UDMMC compact EtherCAT\nmodules that feature two and four universal\ndrives with ratings of 12 Vdc to 80Vdc, and\n2.5A (5A peak) to 20A (40A peak) per drive.\nEach drive is programmable to control a twoor three-phase servomotor, a DC brush motor,\na voice coil motor, and a two- or three-phase\nstep motor. The motor drives address the\nneeds of multi-axis motion applications with\nlimited space.\nThe safe torque off (STO) cuts the power to the motor without\nremoval of the power source for applications that are required to comply with SIL-3 and PLe safety levels. The four-axis modules can be\nordered with mixed current specifications. It is a slave drive that runs\nunder any ACS EtherCAT masters. The MMI Application Studio, a set\nof software support tools, is provided for configuration, setup, tuning,\nand diagnostics.\nFor Free Info Visit http://info.hotims.com/49746-319\n\nLinear Motor Stages\nKollmorgen (Radford, VA) has introduced MMG series linear motor\nstages in four models that\ndeliver 25-mm, 50-mm, 100mm, and 150-mm travel.\nThey provide uncompensated accuracy from 6 um to 14\num, and resolution from 1.0\num to 5 nm. Each model delivers\nrepeatability to \xc2\xb10.4 um, and is rated\nfor 10-kg load capacity. The stages feature an integrated feedback mechanism that eliminates the need for compensation\ntables or slope correction factors. A standard Z-axis counterbalance kit\neliminates the engineering required to integrate a Z option. The stages\nleverage a standard 3-phase brushless motor to enable control with various drives and controllers. No specialized piezo or proprietary\nmotor/drive technology is necessary. They can be used in constant\nvelocity (CV) or high throughput point-to-point applications, allowing\ncommon units to be used.\n\nWorkholding Vice\n\nFor Free Info Visit http://info.hotims.com/49746-315\n\nThe RZM Centric Vice from R\xc3\xb6hm Products of\nAmerica (Lawrenceville, GA) provides workholding rigidity and contributes to higheraccuracy 5-axis machining. The vice\xe2\x80\x99s\ndesign features clamping jaws positioned relatively high, and a horizontal\nspindle situated at the top of the vice and\ncloser to the jaws. The jaws are shorter and complement the vice\xe2\x80\x99s overall compact height of 7.7" to minimize interference.\nThe double jaw-guidance system moves jaws along their axes to accommodate a range of part sizes without having to remount the jaws. In operation, the first jaw moves along an outside guideway as the second jaw\ntravels on an inside one. This quasi-telescopic arrangement allows for a\ngreater guidance length without placing significant limits on machining\noperations. When fully opened, the RZM presents little, if any, interference, and its telescoping design allows the jaws to close to the zero point.\n\nTool Positioning System\nThe EPPINGER Trifix\xc2\xae tool positioning system from\nEXSYS Tool (San Antonio, FL) enables exchanges of\nboth static and driven tooling for multitasking\nmachines. Based on the VDI interface, the system\nprovides positioning accuracy within 10 \xce\xbcm between\ntool stations, and single-position repeatability of less\nthan 5 \xce\xbcm at a tool length of 3.9" (100 mm). After the\nuser initially aligns the unit in the lathe turret, further\nadjustment for subsequent tool changes becomes unnecessary. As a result, manufacturers can preset tools off the machine,\nreducing setup time. Tooling can be mounted with four additional\nhold-down screws to maximize rigidity in heavy-chipload operations\nsuch as milling. Use of the Trifix system does not prevent a facility from\nusing other tooling.\n\nFor Free Info Visit http://info.hotims.com/49746-326\n\n14a\n\nFor Free Info Visit http://info.hotims.com/49746-329\n\nwww.techbriefs.com/motion\n\nIntro\n\nCov\n\nToC\n\n+\n\nMotion Control and Automation Technology, June 2014\n\n\xe2\x80\x93\n\nA\n\n\xe2\x9e\xad\n\n\xe2\x9e\xae\n\n'
